<time>1548725699609</time><Rate>3<//Rate>< Review>
The view from this winery is amazing. I was excited to go into the caves.  It smells of the oak barrels that hold the wine.  It's an unforgettable scent.  I don't like that they charge $7 per person for tasting.  Some of the closer wineries do not charge a tasting fee.  Also, their pricing is a bit over the top. $50 for one bottle. $19.95 each for 2-5 bottles...and it gets less expensive the more you buy.  But if I only want one bottle, I don't want to pay $50 for it!  Today when I went, they only had red wines, which I do not care for.  A variety would be nice. I'm giving 3 stars for the location and view. We bought 2 bottles which was less expensive than buying one.</Review>

< review>
PORT! PORT! PORT!

We come here for the port! I mean the other wines are good too, but holy port batman dont leave without some port. We belong to the port club, but always leave with more ports then we stopped for. We also own a 1 gallon pony keg that is kept full of port at all times. Thanks to Toogood we have become pirates and are constantly pillaging many different ports.

On A side note we recently attended a "private" tasting in the cave. This was a limited seating event and $75 a person. Hands down this is the most fun I have ever had tasting wine. Our guide, Tom; was phenomenal! If you have the time (ours was almost 3 hours) try it!

Also... BUY ALL THE PORT!</review>

<Review>This is not about the wines, but rather about the "special event" we recently attended there; specifically the Spaghetti Dinner, in late March, 2015.
The quality of the meal was ridiculously poor.
Packaged dinner rolls with no flavor or texture.  Tasted like Wonder bread left out too long.
The salad was okay - fairly fresh and green.
The spaghetti "with meat" was just completely terrible.  I do not exaggerate when I say I've had better from a can with a Chef-Boy-R-D label.  The meat sauce was more like unseasoned sloppy-joe mix, and I honestly thought someone had just used a potato masher on some old meatloaf, and then mixed it with water and ketchup.  The pasta was overcooked (or cooked yesterday) mush and without any texture or flavor.  The plate reminded me of school cafeteria fare, ...and that is being unkind to school cafeteria cooks.
The dessert included a very stale ladyfinger biscuit on a plate with some blueberries (which were wrinkled and well past their "freshness" window).
All of that for about $30 per person, and not even a complimentary glass of wine.
Never again.  These folks should stick to wine-making, hire a chef, or have these things catered by someone who has a clue.
Good lord.

FRAUD
After being told the dealer changed staff and management I decided to give them another go.
My vehicle was brought to them on 2 occasions for rim and tire damage. The dealer was provided the insurance companies details along with the claim number. I was told, on both occasions that the insurance company does not cover said damage.  After the second claim denial I contacted my insurance company for clarity and they explained neither claim was ever followed up on by the dealer and the first simply expired. This is legally referenced as INSURANCE FRAUD.  In addition to the lie on the claim they insisted I would also need to buy new tires as they can't out mine on new rims due to the wear.   I contacted Alfa USA and was directed to another dealer.  They called on the claims and the rim damage was fully covered.  Additionally, the tires were confirmed to be just fine.

My 90 day old Alfa was presented to the dealer as the infotainment screen looses.connection.(infotainment screen displays the Radio climate control and parking sensors). Recognizing the issue they replaced the feature neglecting to activate my Satellite service (not a huge deal but detail matters as fixing that required another service appointment at a dealer that does not provide loaners). The infotainment went out again the following week (the first time I got in the car since the original service) and the vehicle was submitted again for a needed software update. Unfortunately, the next day the system crashed again. The service rep suggested the USB feature is causing the issue and suggested I stop using it.   As this was not an acceptable suggestion I requested they fix it. When requesting to speak with management as I am aware the service agent has protocol he needs to follow, the representative would not connect me to management and simply suggested sourcing another dealer.

Terrible in every way. It's pricy, dingy and oddly laid out, forces you to use a card rather than quarters (though, of course, you still have to load that card with cash. < review>
This nursery is the type of place you drive by every day and don't realize it until you are looking for a hard-to-find plant or tree.

The staff is very knowledgable but the plants are not always in the best condition. This is not a deal breaker for me. With a little love and attention, a not so pretty plant or tree will become beautiful.

The prices will definitely give you sticker shock. If you are looking for a one of a kind plant or tree, give them a call first. Chances are they will have what you are looking for.< /review>

I always recommend this place to new gardeners who move into the area.  They will guide you to plants that are appropriate for your location and needs.  A few times I have come here looking for specific plants and they warned me about a pest/disease/other problem in the area and then pointed out other options that were better suited locally. <Time>1530391845926<//Time>< Review>
I don't know about you, but legal mumbo jumbo gives me the heebie-jeebies, which is why I pay an accountant to do my taxes and made my husband figure out the highly-complicated immigration paperwork when I was bringing him over from Canada. The same goes for student loans; they are a headache and a half! As ASLA aptly acknowleges: "most individuals find this process difficult and confusing"--even those of us with master's degrees in nonfiction writing, which is of course which brought me to ASLA in the first place.

The point is, ASLA makes the process easy and idiot-proof, and Operations Manager Nicole Marroquin in particular has been a gem to work with over the past two years. I have referred her a number of times to others in need and plan to refer her to my husband when he finishes his teaching credential.

Thanks, ASLA and Nicole for keeping me heebie-jeeby free, so to speak. I'm forever indebted to you, as you work to chip away at my student debt. :)</Review>

< review>
Went there to buy 2 dozen popsicles, two large mangonadas, 2 large drinks and one frescas con crema. Over $70 later, found out that they don't even have a box for the 26 popsicles that I purchased which were melted by the time I came home. Since the plastic covering the ice cream is open at the bottom, when they melted, they spilled all over the plastic bag that she stuffed all of them in. What a waste!

I asked for a cover for the mangonada and I was told that the cup is too large for the cover. Strange, we were just there last weekend and I got a cover for the large then.

The checkout girl's response... "No one ever complains". Really??? Don't they want people to buy a lot of their ice cream? We thought it would be nice to support a local business and their success, but to be honest, this will be our last visit there. The customer service was uncaring and terrible.  She definitely went out of her way to let me know that they don't care about how their customers feel.< /review>
